<h2 class="title">The Wire</h2>
<div class="headline-block-wrapper">
<div class="img-wrapper">

<li>
<a class="article-title" href="#article_0">New tunnel, premium RV section at Talladega Superspeedway on schedule despite weather</a>
<div class="article-content-wrapp" id="article_0">
<div class="article-excerpt">
<div class="text-small">
<p>Excerpt:</p>
<blockquote><p>Construction of a new oversized vehicle tunnel and premium RV infield parking section at Talladega Superspeedway is still on schedule to be completed in time for the April NASCAR race, despite large amounts of rainfall and unusual groundwater conditions underneath the track.</p>
<p>Track Chairman Grant Lynch, during a news conference Wednesday at the track, said he’s amazed the general contractor, Taylor Corporation of Oxford, has been able to keep the project on schedule.</p>
<p>“The amount of water they have pumped out of that and the extra engineering they did from the original design, basically to keep that tunnel from floating up out of the earth, was remarkable,” Lynch said.</p>
</blockquote></div>
</div>

<li>
<a class="article-title" href="#article_0">Alabama workers built 1.6M engines in 2018 to add auto horsepower</a>
<div class="article-content-wrapp" id="article_0">
<div class="article-excerpt">
<div class="text-small">
<p>Excerpt:</p>
<blockquote><p>Alabama’s auto workers built nearly 1.6 million engines last year, as the state industry continues to carve out a place in global markets with innovative, high-performance parts, systems and finished vehicles.</p>
<p>Last year also saw major new developments in engine manufacturing among the state’s key players, and more advanced infrastructure is on the way in the coming year.</p>
<p>Hyundai expects to complete a key addition to its engine operations in Montgomery during the first half of 2019, while Honda continues to reap the benefits of a cutting-edge Alabama engine line installed several years ago.</p>
</blockquote></div>

<div class="author-options">
<a class="author url fn" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/author/dennis-washington/" rel="author" title="Posts by Dennis Washington">Dennis Washington</a>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama company enhances environment with pandemic-friendly project</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Evonik-Corporation-Environmental-Health-Safety-Brian-Bennett.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Dennis Washington/Alabama NewsCenter)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>A Mobile business has found a way for their employees to help the environment amid <a href="https://alabamanewscenter.com/coronavirus/">COVID-19</a> restrictions on normal volunteer activities.</p>
<p><a href="http://mobile.evonik.us/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Evonik Corporation</a> (EC) recently built and deployed more than 70 bird boxes on its property in Mobile County. EC Logistics Manager Helen Bush says the idea came about during a <a href="https://pepmobile.org/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Partners for Environmental Progress</a> membership meeting last fall.</p>
<p>“We watched a member talk about their quest to be certified for a National Wildlife Habitat Council project,” Bush said. “I realized we were already doing a lot of the same things so I looked at how joining that program could make our projects more meaningful to the Mobile community and natural wildlife here.”</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            405</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">405 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-company-enhances-environment-with-pandemic-friendly-project/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">405 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p><iframe allowfullscreen="allowfullscreen" frameborder="0" height="360" src="https://player.vimeo.com/video/521504401?color=eb2031" width="640"></iframe></p>
<p><a href="https://vimeo.com/521504401">Evonik Corporation builds bird habitats</a> from <a href="https://vimeo.com/alabamanewscenter">Alabama NewsCenter</a> on <a href="https://vimeo.com">Vimeo</a>.</p>
<p>Bush and other department leaders settled on a project to replace more than 70 bird boxes on EC property. The boxes, constructed years ago to enhance habitats for bluebirds and ducks, had deteriorated.</p>
<p>“One of the projects we did in the past was to build natural habitats for birds – ducks, bluebirds, purple martins and osprey,” Bush said. “We realized some of our birdhouses needed to be replaced.”</p>
<p>Because COVID-19 restrictions prevented company employees from voluntarily gathering together to assemble the boxes, Bush enlisted the help of the company’s maintenance department to create a kit employees could take home. EC Water Compliance Specialist Chris Bolling said employees quickly signed up.</p>
<p>“We were very amazed we got that many volunteers,” Bolling said. “It’s good to see an industrial company cares about the environment and is willing to involve their employees to do something like this. It’s really been fun.”</p>
<p>“I didn’t even get one,” added Bush. “We ran out. People were eager to get one.”</p>
<p>The boxes were installed throughout the company property in January and February. EC Environmental Health and Safety Specialist Brian Bennett said employees are excited to see them.</p>
<p>“We actually had more people calling and asking when could we build more, when are you going to do this again,” Bennett said. “It’s been great so far. Just being involved in putting them out and then starting to see the birds interested in them, getting closer and closer and then starting to use the boxes – it really shows the importance of that to the company and to the employees.”</p>
<p>Bush said plans are underway to replace aging osprey nests and artificial habitats for bats and purple martins on EC property. She said the new osprey nests will need to be mounted on taller poles to get them higher than surrounding trees. Bush looks forward to resuming normal volunteer activities after the pandemic, but admits this project has been fun.</p>
<p>“It has been nice in a year where we haven’t been able to see each other every day to be able to do something for each other and for the site that enhances not only the environmental benefit we can make but also something the employees enjoy doing,” Bush said. “Hopefully it’s more beneficial for the birds but it has been a lot of fun for us and pretty rewarding.”</p>
<p><em>(Courtesy of <a href="https://alabamanewscenter.com/2021/03/23/alabama-company-enhances-environment-with-pandemic-friendly-project/">Alabama NewsCenter</a>)</em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>‘God was with all these people, and us’: Amid tornado destruction, cross stands tall</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Eagle-Point-wooden-cross-tornado.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Derek Van Dam/Twitter)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>One Shelby County family has found their faith in God strengthened after a tornado tore through their Eagle Point neighborhood on Thursday, <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aMr1qwp-sSk">severely damaging</a> their home and several others.</p>
<p><a href="https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/26/us/alabama-tornado-cross-trnd/index.html">CNN</a> reported that Dena Cook and her husband “rode out the tornado in a closet in their two-story home” and “could see the storm clouds above them when the roof gave way.” The tornado has been preliminarily rated as at least an EF-3.</p>
<p>It was, perhaps, a miracle that no one died in Eagle Point on Thursday, as Cook’s story underscores.</p>
<p>Last year, her husband reportedly constructed a wooden cross in their backyard. Cook recently draped this wooden cross with a purple cloth for Lent.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            129</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">129 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/god-was-with-all-these-people-and-us-amid-tornado-destruction-cross-stands-tall/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">129 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>As she emerged from her battered home on Thursday, there was the cross — still resolutely standing — and the purple cloth — still hugging the cross.</p>
<p>“It’s just God,” Cook told <a href="https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/26/us/alabama-tornado-cross-trnd/index.html">CNN</a> on Friday. “It’s still there and my cross is still there, because God was with all these people, and us.”</p>
<p>For Easter next Sunday, Cook plans to replace the purple cloth with a white one.</p>
<p>“This is what God is all about,” Cook reportedly said while pointing to the cross. “Lent is a sorrowful time but then on that Easter Sunday, it will be beautiful all again.”</p>
<figure aria-describedby="caption-attachment-158646" class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_158646" style="width: 225px"><a href="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Exak8qAXEAoRJqd.jpg"><img alt="" class="size-medium wp-image-158646" height="300" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 225px) 100vw, 225px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Exak8qAXEAoRJqd-225x300.jpg" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Exak8qAXEAoRJqd-225x300.jpg 225w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Exak8qAXEAoRJqd-768x1024.jpg 768w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Exak8qAXEAoRJqd-1152x1536.jpg 1152w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Exak8qAXEAoRJqd.jpg 1536w" width="225"/></a><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-158646">Dena Cook (Derek Van Dam/Twitter)</figcaption></figure>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Chart Industries plans Alabama growth project, creating 94 jobs</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Chart-Industries-Mobile.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Chart Industries/Contributed)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>MOBILE, Alabama — Georgia-based <a href="https://www.chartindustries.com/">Chart Industries</a>, a leading maker of equipment used in the clean energy and industrial gas markets, plans a $2.5 million investment in an expansion project that will create 94 jobs at its Alabama facility, according to the <a href="https://mobilechamber.com/">Mobile Area Chamber</a>.</p>
<p>The project is expected to more than double the manufacturing capacity of hydrogen transport trailers at the Theodore facility and introduce the capability of producing hydrogen bulk storage tanks at the Mobile County site.</p>
<p>“The Mobile community is a great place for us to expand our business in part due to the accessibility of the Port of Mobile but more importantly, the highly-skilled talent that we are eager to add to the Chart family,” Chart CEO and President Jill Evanko said.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            290</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">290 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/chart-industries-plans-alabama-growth-project-creating-94-jobs/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">290 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>In October 2020, Chart purchased the hydrogen trailer and cryogenic trailer business of Worthington Industries, which operated the Theodore site. Chart’s new investment will improve the existing facility, construct a new building and purchase needed equipment.</p>
<p>“Chart is another example of a company that sees value in our area workforce and the community’s logistical assets that include the Port of Mobile,” said David Rodgers, the Mobile Area Chamber’s vice president of economic development.</p>
<p>“Our manufacturing sector continues to grow and prosper in our community.”</p>
<p>GROWTH PLANS</p>
<p>The Chamber said Chart will add 94 jobs over two years at the Theodore facility while also retaining 41 jobs.</p>
<p>“The City of Mobile is proud to support the expansion of Chart Industries to bring 94 new jobs to the area and double their capacity in Mobile,” Mayor Sandy Stimpson said.</p>
<p>“This investment by the company will have a significant impact on the local economy by diversifying our manufacturing industry and supporting local vendors. Congratulations to Chart Industries on this important step towards many years of success here in Mobile.”</p>
<p>Hydrogen is widely used today in petroleum refining, technology and fertilizer production while it is taking on a greater role with fuel cells for distribution centers, for companies like Walmart and Amazon.</p>
<p>“When a business downsizes or vacates an area, there is a negative the community has to adjust to. So, I am relieved and thrilled that Chart Industries purchased the industrial products portion of Worthington Industries in Theodore,” Mobile County Commissioner Randall Dueitt said.</p>
<p>Chart is a publicly traded company based in Ball Ground, Ga., just outside of Atlanta. It was named one of Fortune’s 100 Fastest Growing Companies in 2020, and it has customers on six continents. The Theodore location is its only site in Alabama.</p>
<p><em>(Courtesy of <a href="https://www.madeinalabama.com/2021/03/chart-industries-plans-alabama-growth-project-creating-94-jobs/">Made in Alabama</a>)</em></p>
</p>

<a class="view-less1" href="javascript:void(0)">

</a>
</div>

<div class="author-logo" style="background-image: url(https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/themes/techmag-child/assets/images/yellowhammernews-icon.png);"></div>
<div class="author-options">

<span>4 hours ago</span>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>State Rep. Blackshear: As comprehensive on gaming as we can be, the better off we’re going to be</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Blackshear.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Facebook)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>State Sen. Del Marsh’s (R-Anniston) comprehensive gaming proposal will reportedly get a second look next week when lawmakers return from their spring break recess. Marsh’s effort tried earlier in the session came up two votes short of the three-fifths required for a constitutional amendment.</p>
<p>While most of the action of gaming has been in the legislature’s upper chamber, the House of Representatives has yet to consider any gaming legislation this session. However, Marsh’s effort seems to have some support in the House.</p>
<p>State Rep. Chris Blackshear (R-Phenix City) told Mobile radio’s FM Talk 106.5 on Friday that he sees the comprehensive approach superior to a piecemeal approach to gaming, which would have the separate components — lottery, sports betting and casino gaming — be considered separately.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            531</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">531 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/state-rep-blackshear-as-comprehensive-on-gaming-as-we-can-be-the-better-off-were-going-to-be/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">531 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p><iframe frameborder="0" height="300" scrolling="no" src="https://embeds.audioboom.com/posts/7831325/embed/v4" style="background-color: transparent; display: block; padding: 0; max-width: 700px;" title="Audioboom player" width="100%"></iframe></p>
<p>“Well, first off, I’ll preface that by saying my grandfather, who passed away 20 years ago, was a Baptist minister for 40 years,” he said. “So, a Baptist minister for 40 years in the state of Alabama, what I’m about to say would probably, if he were sitting here, would take me out back and try to choke me out. But I think as comprehensive, Jeff, as we can be, the better off we’re going to be because I think there’s a couple of things — you know you have to play the fact-of-fiction card with this. Everyone hears, you know, the Poarch Creek have a monopoly. No, they don’t have a monopoly. Currently, they’re protected on the federal land, but they do have the only casinos because of our state constitution. Well, I think if you make it comprehensive, you have an opportunity to pull them in with a compact, then you start pulling some money in from them.”</p>
<p>“I’m prefacing this off of Senator Marsh’s bill that he has laid out because that’s really the only one that we’ve seen,” Blackshear continued. “As I walk through this, that’s kind of what I’m using as a blueprint here. The way his legislation was is you’d be pulling money from the Poarch Creeks that the state’s never gotten before. It would also enable the other dog tracks that have really been through a battle for multiple reasons over the last 20-25 years to operate if they choose to pay a license and have an ownership at one of these Class 3 gaming locations. If you cover that, that pulls in additional revenue. Then you have the paper lottery piece, which was going to focus on education. I think as comprehensive as we can be, you’ve got to do that piece, too, for education. You’ve got to bring them in. And then you’ve got the sports gaming piece as well, too. People are driving to other states just to participate in that now.”</p>
<p>“We’re leaving money on the table if we don’t do it comprehensively,” he added. “If we don’t do anything at all, we’re just letting money go to other states to help them, Jeff. So, I’m all for comprehensive on this. But at the same time, before we send it to the people to vote, the enabling legislation truly needs to be spelled out. I think when the citizens who go to vote at the polls, if we ever get to that point, they need to understand what they are voting on exactly, where the money will go if it does pass, how gaming in the state would be legislated and overseen by the commission all the way through.”</p>
<p>The Russell County Republican said House action on the measure was likely contingent on what happened in the Senate next week or if Gov. Kay Ivey were to get involved.</p>
<p><strong><em><a href="http://twitter.com/jeff_poor">@Jeff_Poor</a> is a graduate of Auburn University and the University of South Alabama, the editor of <a href="https://www.breitbart.com/clips">Breitbart TV</a>, a columnist for Mobile’s <a href="https://lagniappemobile.com/category/commentary/beltway/">Lagniappe Weekly</a>, and host of Mobile’s “The Jeff Poor Show” from 9 a.m.-12 p.m. <a href="http://www.fmtalk1065.com/">on FM Talk 106.5</a>.</em></strong></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Tuberville rips COVID-19 ‘relief’ bill — ‘Alabama taxpayers are paying off the bills for San Francisco, Chicago and New York’</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Tommy-Tuberville-floor-speech-maiden.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Senator Tommy Tuberville/YouTube)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Now that Democrats control the U.S. House of Representatives, U.S. Senate and the White House, there is little Republicans can do to slow the massive spending packages that Democrats are poised to push through into law.</p>
<p>Among those is the $2 trillion COVID-19 relief bill, which includes funding for more than just coronavirus-related government programs.</p>
<p>U.S. Sen. Tommy Tuberville (R-Auburn) voiced his frustration about what has been done in the name of COVID-19 relief on Mobile radio FM Talk 106.5’s “The Jeff Poor Show.” He described the legislation as “theft” and said it was Alabama taxpayers that were paying off bills for Democrat cities throughout the country.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            399</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">399 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/tuberville-rips-covid-19-relief-bill-alabama-taxpayers-are-paying-off-the-bills-for-san-francisco-chicago-and-new-york/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">399 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p><iframe frameborder="0" height="300" scrolling="no" src="https://embeds.audioboom.com/posts/7830500/embed/v4" style="background-color: transparent; display: block; padding: 0; max-width: 700px;" title="Audioboom player" width="100%"></iframe></p>
<p>“The best stimulus plan is to open this country up and get people back to work,” he said. “This is ridiculous. This time last year, we were getting into this pandemic, and we thought two or three weeks and open it back up.. ‘Everybody, protect yourself and go to work and save this country, save your family, save yourself.’ And we’ve had all this science come at us, and a lot of it has been good. We have lost a lot of people. That has been a huge problem, very unfortunate. But now it is time to get back to work because we’re losing people because of mental health, because of a lot of things that are coming off of not going to work, not going to school.”</p>
<p>“It is an absolute disaster,” Tuberville continued. “We’ve created more of a disaster for the long run than this pandemic ever thought about. We’ve done it because of the rules and regulations that Joe Biden and his administration and the House and Senate have tried to push. The American people deserve answers for a lot of things, especially the border. Why did they steal this $2 trillion? Now, this is theft. This is not passing it and giving it out. Alabama taxpayers are paying off the bills for San Francisco, Chicago and New York — paying their bills. They can’t pay them themselves. They can’t manage their own money. It’s just an absolute disaster. of what they did with this.”</p>
<p>Tuberville also warned about the forthcoming $3 trillion infrastructure proposal coming from the Biden administration. The freshman U.S. Senator said a tax increase could accompany that measure.</p>
<p>“I’m telling you — this $3 trillion that is coming for infrastructure, which I’m not against infrastructure, but we really better be careful what we’re doing here,” he continued. “We better be accountable. But get ready. Here come the taxes. They’re right behind it. Everybody that said, ‘Well, Joe Biden is not going to raise taxes’ — you’re getting ready to get hit right between the eyes. Their huge tax plan is coming.”</p>
<p><strong><em><a href="http://twitter.com/jeff_poor">@Jeff_Poor</a> is a graduate of Auburn University and the University of South Alabama, the editor of <a href="https://www.breitbart.com/clips">Breitbart TV</a>, a columnist for Mobile’s <a href="https://lagniappemobile.com/category/commentary/beltway/">Lagniappe Weekly</a>, and host of Mobile’s “The Jeff Poor Show” from 9 a.m.-12 p.m. <a href="http://www.fmtalk1065.com/">on FM Talk 106.5</a>.</em></strong></p>
</p>

<div class="author-options">
<a class="author url fn" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/author/david-rainer/" rel="author" title="Posts by David Rainer">David Rainer</a>
<span>7 hours ago</span>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>WFF Enforcement Section teaches handgun basics classes</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Cahaba-Handgun-Safety.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(David Rainer/Contributed)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>As firearms sales continue to set records, the Alabama Wildlife and Freshwater Fisheries (WFF) Division’s Law Enforcement Section recognized a demand in basic training for handgun safety and use. Eight million new gun owners were created in 2020 alone. The COVID-19 pandemic forced many to abandon their usual indoor recreations and take up new ones outdoors. For many that was shooting.</p>
<p>This past weekend, officers of the Law Enforcement Section and its Hunter Education Unit held the first of five “Introduction to Handguns” courses scheduled this spring.</p>
<p>Two sessions were held at the Cahaba River Wildlife Management Area (WMA) Shooting Range in Shelby County with 10 students at each session. The WFF staff covered the basics of firearms safety and marksmanship with new shooters from the area.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            1333</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">1333 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/wff-enforcement-section-teaches-handgun-basics-classes/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">1333 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>“It’s no secret that there has been a surge in firearms sales in the past year,” said Marisa Futral, WFF’s Hunter Education Coordinator, who was joined by Stuart Goldsby, Regional Hunter Education Coordinator in north Alabama. “My office has been getting a lot of phone calls from people who want to know if there are any classes available for new shooters. There’s a huge demand from people who want firearms instruction. We are trying to fill that need by starting with  handgun classes and possibly adding long gun classes in the future. The classes are open to anybody who would like to come, but we are kind of targeting the new users. This could be people who are thinking about purchasing a firearm, or they have already purchased one and need to learn how to use it. They might be timid about going to a shooting range by themselves.”</p>
<p>The next “Introduction to Handguns” classes will be held at the Swan Creek WMA Shooting Range in Limestone County on April 2 and April 17, 2021. The next class at the Cahaba range on April 10 is already booked up, but don’t hesitate to get on the waiting list as future classes at this location are in the works. The last currently scheduled class is at the Etowah WMA Shooting Range near Gadsden on April 24. Contact Futral by phone at 334-242-3620 or email <a href="mailto:marisa.futral@dcnr.alabama.gov" rel="noopener" target="_blank">marisa.futral@dcnr.alabama.gov</a> for more information.</p>
<p>Lead firearms instructor Scott Kellenberger, one of only a handful of Alabama Peace Officers Standards and Training Commission certified master firearms instructors in Alabama, explained to the students the basics of firearms safety – always treat all firearms as if they are loaded; never allow the muzzle of the firearms to cover anything you are not willing to destroy; always keep your trigger finger off the trigger until your sights are on the target and you have made the conscious decision to fire; and always be sure of your target and what is beyond.</p>
<p>After Kellenberger’s safety instructions, the students were each provided with a personal instructor to learn handgun basics with a Ruger .22 caliber semi-automatic handgun. All necessary firearms, ammunition and safety equipment were provided by WFF for the new shooters.</p>
<p>The students learned how to load a magazine and insert it the magazine into the handgun and how to manipulate the safety and slide release. Instructors ensured that the students followed all safety procedures and offered tips on the proper grip for best control of the firearm and accuracy. Students also learned how to clear their firearms after a misfire or a failure-to-eject occurred.</p>
<p>“We try to introduce novice shooters to our (WFF) ranges,” Kellenberger said. “If they are interested, we get them involved in shooting sports. Obviously, we start with firearms safety. Then we talk about range safety. We discuss at length what range etiquette means. A lot of people have never shot on a public range before. They learn how to call the range ‘hot’ or ‘cold’ and how to keep everything safe on the range. For many new shooters, the simple fear of not knowing what is appropriate on one of our ranges can be a barrier to them. After this class, they all completely understand how to use our ranges and what they need to have in reference to a license. Then we move on to stance, grip and trigger control. We go over ammunition selection, dry-firing as a practice technique and then live fire.”</p>
<p>A set of paper targets was set up at 6 yards for students to shoot during the first session. After instruction and practice, the students were able to “ping” metal targets at 25 yards.</p>
<p>Kellenberger said .22-caliber handguns, either semi-automatic or revolver, are excellent firearms for the newcomers to learn the basics. Many of the students get a great deal of knowledge simply from getting the chance to shoot different styles of handguns. Often they go home after a class and purchase the exact handgun that they enjoyed shooting on the range.</p>
<p>“The .22s are great starter guns,” he said. “They can learn all the basics and do it inexpensively. For people who are a little bit afraid of firearms, there is not a lot of recoil and not a loud report. They’re easy to shoot, and the ammo is less expensive. That means a lot right now with ammo being sold in never before seen amounts. A progression a lot of people take is to start with a .22 and then move up to the firearm they are comfortable shooting or carrying if they decide to.”</p>
<p>Kellenberger said he can see changes in the students’ confidence from the start of the class to the end.</p>
<p>“With the volume of shooting and close instruction, they are a lot more comfortable with firearms and shooting than when they got here,” he said. “They were all smiling when they left, which is a good thing.”</p>
<p>To use WFF Public Shooting Ranges, Alabama residents are required to have a valid hunting, wildlife heritage, fishing, or WMA license for all range users between the ages of 16-64. For nonresidents, a valid WMA license or non-resident hunting license is required for all range users age 16 or older.</p>
<p>“All of our shooters today purchased the Wildlife Heritage License before participating,” Kellenberger said. “I explained that this $11 license allows them to use our public shooting ranges and our public archery parks for a year. It allows us (WFF) to provide these services to the citizens of Alabama. WFF does not receive any money from the state’s General Fund, and a large portion of the funding that pays for programs like this comes directly from license sales and matching federal funds.”</p>
<p>As Kellenberger said before, it was all smiles when the class ended, and the participants were happy with their firearms education for the day.</p>
<p>“I think it was an excellent experience,” said Jacqueline Brooks of Montgomery, who was accompanied by her daughter, Jayla. “It gives them a chance to teach you one-on-one and make corrections. They show you the proper stance and how to hold your gun, so it was very exciting. I enjoyed learning how to clear a misfire. Sometimes people’s guns do misfire, and they don’t know what to do. I really enjoyed learning that.”</p>
<p>Jamie Ligon of Hoover said she decided to take the class for two reasons, the COVID-19 restrictions that caused her to seek solace on hikes through the woods and the fact her dog probably would not protect her if a situation occurred.</p>
<p>“Since the virus came around, about the only exercise opportunities are outside,” Ligon said. “I’ve gotten very interested in hiking with my dog. I decided if I encountered a snake I might want to have a way to protect myself. My friend asked me if I was afraid walking around. She knows my dog and said, ‘I know Boris is not going to do anything but kiss them to death.’ I was afraid of handguns and after the class not nearly as much. The instructors were all very knowledgeable. I’m glad I did this. I’m going to recommend this to a friend of mine.”</p>
<p>Patti Grace of Vestavia Hills said she loves camping and decided she needed to learn about firearms for her protection.</p>
<p>“I solo-camp,” Grace said. “Sometimes I boondock, which means I camp out in the boonies without electricity and maybe not much safety. I thought it would be good to know how to use a firearm safely. I’ve never shot anything other than a BB gun when I was 8 years old. This was amazing. My instructor, Stuart, was awesome. I’m kind of addicted to it now. I’m going to have to get all kinds of guns. I think this is so good for the public to have a place to come. The experience was awesome.”</p>
<p><em><strong>David Rainer is an award-winning writer who has covered Alabama’s great outdoors for 25 years. The former outdoors editor at the Mobile Press-Register, he writes for Outdoor Alabama, the website of the Alabama Department of Conservation and Natural Resources.</strong></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Austal USA breaks ground on ‘world-class’ steel manufacturing line at Mobile campus — ‘A treasure for the Gulf Coast’</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Austal-steel-groundbreaking.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">Groundbreaking ceremony for the Steel Manufacturing Line at Austal USA in Mobile, Alabama, Friday, March 26, 2021. (Contributed)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Austal USA on Friday broke ground in Mobile on its steel manufacturing line, positioning the company to start steel production in April 2022. The addition of steel capability ensures Austal will remain a major contributor to the U.S. shipbuilding industrial base for many years to come.</p>
<p>The company is headquartered in Mobile, where Austal USA builds aluminum ships at its state-of-the-art manufacturing facility, such as advanced small surface combatant Independence-variant littoral combat ships and auxiliary expeditionary fast transports.</p>
<p>Just as Austal helped turn Mobile into the nation’s premier location for construction of aluminum ships, Friday’s milestone marked the beginning of a new era that is poised to see the company do the same for steel in the near future.</p>
<p>During World War II, residents of Alabama’s Port City built steel Liberty ships that were critical to the war effort. In the coming years, Austal will look to build and deliver steel ships needed by the U.S. Coast Guard and Navy, per a release from the company.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->

</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/austal-usa-breaks-ground-on-world-class-steel-manufacturing-line-at-mobile-campus-a-treasure-for-the-gulf-coast/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">237 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>“This world-class steel manufacturing line is a treasure for the Gulf Coast, the U.S. Navy and the U.S. Coast Guard that will provide a much needed boost to the defense industrial base and our Nation’s defense,” stated Congressman Jerry Carl (AL-01).</p>
<figure aria-describedby="caption-attachment-158623" class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_158623" style="width: 600px"><a href="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/51005210270_8a5e95cd65_b.jpg"><img alt="" class="wp-image-158623" height="256" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/51005210270_8a5e95cd65_b.jpg" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/51005210270_8a5e95cd65_b.jpg 1024w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/51005210270_8a5e95cd65_b-300x128.jpg 300w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/51005210270_8a5e95cd65_b-768x328.jpg 768w" width="600"/></a><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-158623">Austal USA’s Steel Line Facility rendering (Contributed)</figcaption></figure>
<p>Adding steel shipbuilding capability to Austal’s growing business portfolio comes after the company <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/austal-usa-expands-physical-footprint-in-mobile/">expanded</a> its physical footprint in Mobile last year.</p>
<p>“As demand for the greater and larger Navy and Coast Guard fleets grows, Austal USA is investing to meet those changing requirements,” said Rusty Murdaugh, interim Austal USA president. “We’re investing in our people, we’re investing in our processes and we’re investing in our facilities and capabilities.”</p>
<p>Founded on innovation, effectiveness and efficiency, Austal is set to bring its proven lean manufacturing processes and facility design to the steel shipbuilding market. These processes have helped deliver 24 Alabama-built ships to the Navy in the last nine years. No other shipbuilder comes close to matching that performance.</p>
<p>“Each time we have invested in our facilities, our customers have seen a greater return on their investment,” Murdaugh added. “The steel ships that will come off this line will be the best, most efficient and most affordable steel ships in the Coast Guard and Navy fleets.”</p>
<div class="wp-video" style="width: 960px;"><!--[if lt IE 9]><script>document.createElement('video');</script><![endif]-->
<video class="wp-video-shortcode" controls="controls" height="540" id="video-158614-1" preload="metadata" width="960"><source src="https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/210326-Austal-USA-Steel-Line-Groundbreaking-Animation.mp4.mp4?_=1" type="video/mp4"/><a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/210326-Austal-USA-Steel-Line-Groundbreaking-Animation.mp4.mp4">https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/210326-Austal-USA-Steel-Line-Groundbreaking-Animation.mp4.mp4</a></video></div>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama assesses damage, begins recovery after brutal day of tornadoes</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Tornado-destruction-March-26.jpeg');"></div>
<span class="caption">Rose DeArman stands before destroyed house (Kim Chandler/AP)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>The citizens of Alabama are assessing the damage and banding together to care for one another a day after deadly tornadoes battered the state.</p>
<p>The death toll from the storms stands at five people, all of whom lived in the vicinity of Ohatchee, a small town in northwest Calhoun County.</p>
<p>Damage assessments from the National Weather Service (NWS) and others are ongoing in Jefferson, Shelby, St. Clair, Calhoun, Cherokee, Bibb, Hale, Greene and Sumter Counties.</p>
<p>The NWS has preliminarily <a href="https://twitter.com/NWSBirmingham">confirmed</a> that an EF-3 tornado with 140 mph winds struck Shelby County. The service also confirmed EF-2 level damage in Calhoun County and EF-1 level damage in Pickens County.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            278</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">278 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-assesses-damage-begins-recovery-after-brutal-day-of-tornadoes/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">278 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>EF-3 tornadoes have wind speeds from 136-165 mph, while EF-2s range from 111-135 mph and EF-1s range from 86-110 mph.</p>
<p>Local television newscasts in Alabama and the social media feeds of many of the state’s residents remain filled with images of the destruction from Thursday.</p>
<p>Current estimates say 14 tornadoes touched down in Alabama on Thursday, a number subject to change.</p>
<p>A spokesperson for Governor Kay Ivey said on Friday that “[t]he governor is letting our folks do their work in conducting a thorough assessment,” and that if the damage in Alabama meets the threshold for federal assistance, “Alabamians can count on the governor to apply.”</p>
<p>Local authorities are currently providing ways for citizens to help their neighbors.</p>
<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-dnt="true" data-width="500">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en">First Baptist Church of Columbiana (208 North Main Street) will serve as a collection and distribution center for basic needs in our community tomorrow. Items can be dropped off from 8 a.m. to noon and will be ready for distribution from noon to 5 p.m. <a href="https://t.co/9SHH3uB18M">pic.twitter.com/9SHH3uB18M</a></p>
<p>— Shelby County SO (@ShelbyCountySO) <a href="https://twitter.com/ShelbyCountySO/status/1375533262081249284?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">March 26, 2021</a></p></blockquote>
<p><script async="" charset="utf-8" data-rocketlazyloadscript="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script></p>
<p><em>The following information is listed on the <a href="http://www.calhounema.org/help">Calhoun County Emergency Management Agency’s website</a>:</em></p>
<blockquote><p>Donations will be accepted for the affected communities beginning at 10 AM at the Calhoun County Ag Center.</p>
<p>Donations will be distributed beginning Saturday, March 27 at Ohatchee Senior Center and the Webster’s Chapel Community Center from 8 AM – 4 PM each day.</p>
<p>The Volunteer Reception Center will begin accepting Heavy Equipment Volunteers ONLY today from 12 PM – 4 PM.</p>
<p>We need to make sure we allow time for first responders to clear the affected areas from debris, downed lines utility leaks.</p>
<p>The Volunteer Reception Center will begin accepting general public volunteers on Saturday, March 27 from 8 AM – 4 PM</p></blockquote>
<p>The United Way of Central Alabama is also <a href="https://www.uwca.org/tornado/">taking donations for a relief fund</a> for the victims of the March 25 storms.</p>
<p><strong>RELATED: <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/regions-foundation-donates-100k-in-local-relief-following-alabama-tornadoes/">Regions Foundation donates $100K in local relief following Alabama tornadoes</a></strong></p>
<p><em>Henry Thornton is a staff writer for Yellowhammer News. You can contact him by email: henry@yellowhammernews.com or on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/HenryThornton95">@HenryThornton95.</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Regions Foundation donates $100K in local relief following Alabama tornadoes</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Regions-Bank-March-25-2021-Tornadoes-1.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Regions Foundation/Contributed)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>The Regions Foundation on Friday announced a series of grants totaling $100,000 for organizations coordinating disaster relief in portions of Alabama and Georgia that were impacted in the past two days by severe weather, including deadly tornadoes.</p>
<p>The foundation is a nonprofit initiative of Birmingham-headquartered <a href="https://www.regions.com/personal-banking">Regions Bank</a> and supports community investments.</p>
<p>“Many of our communities face a long and difficult recovery, and Regions Bank and the Regions Foundation will be here to offer support and guidance every step of the way,” stated John Turner, president and CEO of Regions Financial Corp.</p>
<p>From the $100,000 total, grants will be issued to the following relief organizations:</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            302</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">302 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/regions-foundation-donates-100k-in-local-relief-following-alabama-tornadoes/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">302 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<blockquote><p>American Red Cross—The Regions Foundation will provide $75,000 to the Alabama and Georgia chapters of the American Red Cross to support relief for people impacted by the storms in areas including metro Birmingham, as well as communities in and near metro Atlanta.</p>
<p>United Way of East Central Alabama—The Regions Foundation will provide $25,000 to United Way of East Central Alabama’s Tornado Relief Fund to help people in places including Ohatchee and other communities in Calhoun and Randolph counties that were struck by a violent storm.</p></blockquote>
<p>At least five people died in Alabama from <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/five-deaths-confirmed-so-far-as-reports-of-tornadoes-storms-flash-floods-pour-in-from-across-central-and-north-alabama/">Thursday’s severe weather.</a></p>
<p>“We mourn the loss of life and recognize the devastating impact the storms had on our neighbors, our communities and our associates,” Turner concluded. “We stand ready to deliver not only the types of financial services that can make the recovery easier, but also the care and compassion of a team that is focused on helping our communities recover and rebuild.”</p>
<p>In addition to the foundation donation, Regions Bank is providing a series of financial services that are available to help people and businesses in portions of Alabama and Georgia that were impacted by the tornado outbreak.</p>
<p>According to a release, those services include:</p>
<blockquote><p>No check-cashing fees for FEMA-issued checks cashed in a branch<br/>
Regions Mortgage Disaster Relief Purchase and Renovation loan programs<br/>
Personal and business loan payment assistance</p></blockquote>
<p>Regions teams are also available to listen to customers’ unique needs and connect them with other options that can help.</p>
<p>“Our community has experienced great loss and destruction, but we have also been inspired to see neighbors helping neighbors in every possible way,” said Linda Jenkins, Calhoun County market executive for Regions Bank. “Support and services from the Regions Foundation and Regions Bank will help our neighbors throughout the recovery process.”</p>
<p><em>Sean Ross is the editor of Yellowhammer News. You can follow him on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/sean_yhn">@sean_yhn</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama nearing 1 million citizens receiving vaccine dose; Eligibility for all coming soon</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Harris-March-26.jpeg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Henry Thornton/YHN)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>MONTGOMERY — If current trends hold, the one-millionth Alabamian to receive a COVID-19 vaccine dose will be reported by the Alabama Department of Public Health in the next two days, and all adults in the state will soon be eligible, according to the Yellowhammer State’s top doctor.</p>
<p>Alabama State Health Officer Dr. Scott Harris briefed the public on the state’s vaccination process at the Alabama Department of Public Health (ADPH) office in Montgomery.</p>
<p>“We are going to be able to expand eligibility [to all adults] well before May 1,” said Harris on Friday, adding that his department was in “discussions with the governor’s office” on the subject.</p>
<p>President Joe Biden, earlier in 2021, established May 1 as the goal for all American adults to be eligible for the vaccines.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            491</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">491 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-nearing-1-million-citizens-receiving-vaccine-dose-eligibility-for-all-coming-soon/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">491 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>A handful of states have already opened up eligibility to all citizens, and another group has announced March or April dates for when all citizens will be eligible for the vaccines. All told, more than 40 states <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/24/us/covid-vaccine-eligibility.html?smid=url-share">have committed</a> to beating Biden’s May 1 deadline.</p>
<p><a href="https://alpublichealth.maps.arcgis.com/apps/MapSeries/index.html?appid=d84846411471404c83313bfe7ab2a367">ADPH’s coronavirus dashboard</a> currently reports 985,078 Alabamians have received at least one dose of the vaccines, which is more than 20% of the state’s population.</p>
<p>The most recent data available is from Wednesday, March 24, meaning Alabama’s millionth person to receive a vaccine dose has likely already gotten their shot.</p>
<p>Currently, 581,714 citizens of Alabama have completed their vaccination process.</p>
<p>In the case of those receiving Pfizer and Moderna’s vaccine products, this means someone has gotten both of the two doses required.</p>
<p>For people receiving Johnson &amp; Johnson’s vaccine, which is only one dose, they complete their vaccination immediately.</p>
<p>Authorities advise that it takes around two weeks after a person’s final dose of any of the vaccines before their body is considered fully vaccinated.</p>
<p>Harris said that Alabama is now receiving around 110,000 doses of vaccine product every week.</p>
<p>He also noted that the state has been informed that it will receive two temporary boosts in its supply next week, one of Pfizer’s vaccine and the other of Johnson &amp; Johnson’s. The two extra allotments will bring the state’s doses received to 156,730 for the week.</p>
<p>“The real issue is going to be to get people to take it,” lamented Harris.</p>
<p>“The script is going to flip completely from a month ago when people couldn’t find the vaccine no matter how hard they looked,” Harris explained. “In April, we’re going to have the opposite problem.”</p>
<p>“We’re going to have a lot of vaccine on the shelf and we’re going to be really trying hard to get people to take it,” Alabama’s top doctor added.</p>
<p>A poll released by ADPH relayed that some amount of hesitancy exists among nearly all demographic groups in Alabama, with the most cited factor being the “speed with which the vaccine was developed.”</p>
<p>Nearly all doctors around the country have taken the vaccine, according to a report from the publication <a href="https://www.medicaleconomics.com/view/physicians-highly-accepting-of-covid-19-vaccine">Medical Economics.</a></p>
<p>This result appears to indicate a high level of trust in the vaccines among the people many citizens turn to most often with their health care decisions.</p>
<p>Notably, Harris himself has received the vaccine, as has former President <a href="https://www.webmd.com/vaccines/covid-19-vaccine/news/20210317/trump-urges-americans-get-covid-vaccine">Donald Trump</a>.</p>
<p>All three vaccine products were tested in studies with tens of thousands of people; all three were completely effective at preventing hospitalization and death from COVID-19.</p>
<p>Around 126 million doses of the vaccines have now been given in the United States. A <a href="https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/vaccines/safety/adverse-events.html">review</a> showed that the vaccines have caused zero deaths.</p>
<p>The CDC is currently reporting that there have been around 30 million cases of COVID-19 in the USA, which has led to <a href="https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#cases_totalcases">543,975 deaths</a>, including <a href="https://bamatracker.com/">10,523</a> Alabamians, as of Friday afternoon.</p>
<p><em>Henry Thornton is a staff writer for Yellowhammer News. You can contact him by email: henry@yellowhammernews.com or on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/HenryThornton95">@HenryThornton95.</a></em></p>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Alabama unemployment falls again, drops to 4% in February</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/08/Alabama-Jobs-Employment-Working-Hired.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(YHN/Pixabay)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Alabama’s unemployment rate has now fallen for both of the first two months of 2021, with February’s rate decreasing to 4.0%.</p>
<p>The Alabama Department of Labor (ADOL) announced the news in a release on Friday morning. In January, Alabama’s unemployment rate was 4.3%.</p>
<p>The 4% unemployment rate reported Friday is still above the 2.6% rate the state enjoyed in February 2020, the last month before the coronavirus pandemic took hold in Alabama.</p>
<p>“The unemployment rate continues to drop and is getting closer to the lows we enjoyed pre-pandemic. While this is good news, the number of unemployed people is still higher than last year,” ADOL Secretary Fitzgerald Washington said in a statement.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            198</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">198 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/alabama-unemployment-falls-again-drops-to-4-in-february/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">198 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>According to numbers provided by ADOL, Alabama had 91,065 unemployed persons seeking work in February. The state had 97,725 in the same position in January.</p>
<p>“Employment assistance is the key to helping reduce this number, and the Alabama Career Center System can help. There are 52 locations around the state that can help the unemployed and the underemployed,” remarked Washington.</p>
<p>The counties with the lowest unemployment rate in January were Shelby (2.1%), Blount and Cullman (2.2%), and Franklin and Limestone (2.3%).</p>
<figure aria-describedby="caption-attachment-158548" class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_158548" style="width: 400px"><a href="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/February-map.jpg" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><img alt="" class="wp-image-158548" height="518" loading="lazy" sizes="(max-width: 400px) 100vw, 400px" src="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/February-map-232x300.jpg" srcset="https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/February-map-232x300.jpg 232w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/February-map-791x1024.jpg 791w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/February-map-768x994.jpg 768w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/February-map-1187x1536.jpg 1187w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/February-map-1583x2048.jpg 1583w, https://s8r5hym581-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/February-map.jpg 1700w" width="400"/></a><figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-158548">(ADOL)</figcaption></figure>
<p>Cities performing best were the suburbs of Birmingham and Huntsville, such as Alabaster and Madison.</p>
<p>The worst performing counties in the state are in the Black Belt region of Alabama. Both Wilcox and Lowndes Counties suffered from unemployment rates of over 11% in February.</p>
<p>Speaking on Alabama’s statewide results, Washington noted, “As COVID cases go down and vaccinations increase, we hope to see improvements in all industries. In addition, as travel picks up and thoughts turn to vacations, the leisure and hospitality industry should see their numbers looking even better.”</p>
<p><em>Henry Thornton is a staff writer for Yellowhammer News. You can contact him by email: henry@yellowhammernews.com or on Twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/HenryThornton95">@HenryThornton95.</a></em></p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>Jill Biden postpones Alabama visit</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/Jill-Biden.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(Wikicommons)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>First lady Jill Biden, Ph.D., will no longer visit Alabama on Friday, according to her office.</p>
<p>Biden was originally <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/whats-in-your-wallet-hollywoods-jennifer-garner-to-join-jill-biden-in-alabama-on-friday/">set to visit</a> the Jasper Area Family Service Center and the YMCA of Central Alabama in Birmingham. Actress Jennifer Garner was slated to accompany the first lady.</p>
<p>“Due to the severe weather across the South and tragic loss of life in Alabama, the First Lady and Jennifer Garner are postponing their trip to Birmingham and Jasper,” said a statement from Biden’s office.</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            140</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">140 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/jill-biden-postpones-alabama-visit/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">140 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p>At least five people died in the Yellowhammer State on Thursday <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/five-deaths-confirmed-so-far-as-reports-of-tornadoes-storms-flash-floods-pour-in-from-across-central-and-north-alabama/">as severe weather battered</a> much of the state.</p>
<p>“Thinking of everyone in Alabama and all of those impacted by the severe weather across the South tonight. My prayers are with the grieving families. Please stay safe,” the first lady <a href="https://twitter.com/FLOTUS/status/1375247698312491009?s=20">tweeted</a> on Thursday evening.</p>
<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en">Thank you, First Lady Biden. We greatly appreciate your concern and prayers. It’s been a devastating day for Alabama, but we will get through this together. <a href="https://twitter.com/FLOTUS?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@FLOTUS</a> <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/alpolitics?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">#alpolitics</a> <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/alwx?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">#alwx</a> <a href="https://t.co/ZPJTqG8NmQ">https://t.co/ZPJTqG8NmQ</a></p>
<p>— Governor Kay Ivey (@GovernorKayIvey) <a href="https://twitter.com/GovernorKayIvey/status/1375283935962406913?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">March 26, 2021</a></p></blockquote>

<p>Biden and Garner were scheduled to stump for the recently enacted $1.9 trillion Democratic spending bill. A new visit date has not yet been announced.</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>7 Things: Severe weather rocks Alabama, Biden holds first press conference, Shelby and Manchin say no national voting overhaul and more …</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/7Things-Daily-New-Friday.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption"></span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p><strong>7. The spending binge is not over</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>People who love spending taxpayer dollars never ever let a crisis go to waste. The “climate change crisis” is a never-ending piggybank of opportunity, and they now want to use it to spend an additional $3 trillion over the next decade, but it could be up to $10 trillion.</li>
<li>Progressives in Congress want to see more spending, higher taxes and a long commitment to spending this money long after President Joe Biden leaves the White House, but they need the filibuster gone to pull most of it off.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>6. Tuberville continues work on southern border crisis </strong></p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            799</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">799 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/7-things-severe-weather-rocks-alabama-biden-holds-first-press-conference-shelby-and-manchin-say-no-national-voting-overhaul-and-more/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">799 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">New legislation introduced by U.S. Senator Tommy Tuberville (R-AL) would <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/tuberville-introduces-bill-to-bar-illegal-aliens-from-receiving-free-pass-into-the-united-states/">require</a> immigrants coming to the southern border illegally at least receive a court date before they’re released into the United States. </span></li>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">This is in response to reports that many illegal immigrants are being released regularly without court dates. This legislation requires the Department of Homeland Security (DHS) give people a Notice to Appear in court. Tuberville has pointed out that releasing people without court dates means that there’s very little way to actually know who is being released into the country.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>5. Amazon has finally responded to Sanders ahead of his Alabama visit</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>U.S. Senator Bernie Sanders (I-VT) is set to visit employees at the Amazon fulfillment center in Bessemer, Alabama today, and just ahead of his trip, Dave Clark, CEO of Amazon’s worldwide consumer business, has <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/amazon-exec-while-bernie-sanders-talks-about-a-15-minimum-wage-we-actually-provide-it-should-save-his-finger-wagging-lecture-until-after-he-actually-delivers/">responded</a> to some of the criticisms from Sanders.</li>
<li>Clark did say that he appreciates Sanders’ “push for a progressive workplace,” but added, “I often say we are the Bernie Sanders of employers, but that’s not quite right because we actually deliver a progressive workplace.” He went on to point out of Amazon has a $15 minimum wage and numerous benefits that Sanders pushes for but has been unable to deliver on.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>4. Georgia becomes one of the first states to change election laws after 2020 election </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>A new law in Georgia has just been <a href="https://www.al.com/news/2021/03/georgia-election-restrictions-signed-into-law-by-gov-brian-kemp-despite-outcry.html">signed</a> by Governor Brian Kemp that will put some restrictions on voting by mail. Despite protests from voter rights groups, the legislation is meant to secure the election process and avoid issues that were seen in the 2020 general election.</li>
<li>Protesters, including State Representatives Park Cannon (D-GA) and Erica Thomas (D-GA), came to Kemp’s office after he signed the bill. There have been claims that this legislation will impact voters of color more than their white counterparts, and Senate Minority Leader Gloria Butler (D-GA) stated, “We are witnessing right now a massive and unabashed assault on voting rights unlike anything we’ve seen since the Jim Crow era.”</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>3. Shelby won’t be supporting HR1, nor will Manchin</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">In the House, H.R. 1, the so-called “For the People Act,” <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/shelby-democrats-attempting-blatant-power-grab-in-an-effort-to-force-a-federalized-election-system/">received</a> no Republican support, and even now U.S. Senator Joe Manchin (D-WV) has shown opposition to the legislation. He said, “Pushing through legislation of this magnitude on a partisan basis may garner short-term benefits, but will inevitably only exacerbate the distrust that millions of Americans harbor against the U.S. government.”</span></li>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">U.S. Senator Richard Shelby (R-AL) has released a statement on the legislation, calling it “a blatant power grab in an effort to force a federalized election system on the entire country.”</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>2. Biden stays upright but struggles to talk filibuster, border crisis, reelection </strong></p>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">President Joe Biden used <a href="https://dailycaller.com/2021/03/25/chris-wallace-joe-biden-white-house-talking-points-foreign-policy-question/">cheat</a> <a href="https://nypost.com/2021/03/25/biden-used-cheat-sheet-during-his-first-press-conference/">sheets</a> and looked pretty <a href="https://dailycaller.com/2021/03/25/joe-biden-seemed-to-float-away-press-conference/">bad</a>, but held his first press conference with a very <a href="https://www.mrctv.org/videos/clown-show-wh-press-corps-embarrass-themselves-biden-presser#.YFziX3-Nlvw.twitter">friendly</a> media on Thursday. He <a href="https://www.foxnews.com/politics/biden-news-conference-ending-trump-era-migrant-protocols">covered</a> a range of issues, including supporting changes for the filibuster. Biden said that he believes “we should go back to a position of a filibuster that existed just when I came to the United States Senate 120 years ago.” He also said that “it used to be that from between 1917 and 1971 the filibuster existed, there were a total of 58 motions to break a filibuster. … Last year alone, there were five times that many. So, it’s being abused in a gigantic way.”</span></li>
<li><span style="color: #222222;">When discussing the immigration crisis at the southern border, Biden said that the Trump era “policies that were underway were not helping at all, did not slow the amount of immigration. Rolling back the policies of separating children from their mothers? Make no apology for that.” Later in the press conference, Biden said that it was his “expectation” to run for reelection in 2024 with Vice President Kamala Harris. When asked if he thought former President Donald Trump would run as a Republican, Biden said, “I have no idea … I have no idea if there will be a Republican Party.”</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>1. At least 5 dead in severe weather outbreak</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>A severe weather system <a href="https://yellowhammernews.com/five-deaths-confirmed-so-far-as-reports-of-tornadoes-storms-flash-floods-pour-in-from-across-central-and-north-alabama/">spawned</a> tornados, heavy rains and floods from the Black Belt, across the Birmingham metro and into North Alabama dealing out property <a href="https://www.al.com/news/2021/03/shelby-county-storm-damage-no-injuries-reported-buildings-damaged-us-280-blocked-by-trees.html">damage</a>, power outages and death. Five people are confirmed dead in Calhoun County’s Ohatchee.</li>
<li>Governor Kay Ivey issued a statement noting the severity of this destruction. She said, “Significant and dangerous weather continues to impact portions of Alabama, and I urge all folks in the path of these tornadoes and storm systems to remain on high alert. Tragically, we are receiving reports of loss of life.” Even famed meteorologist James Spann’s house was <a href="https://www.al.com/news/birmingham/2021/03/james-spann-tells-viewers-his-house-damaged-by-alabama-tornado-texts-wife-and-returns-to-air.html">hit</a> while he was on the air.</li>
</ul>
</p>

<div class="post-title">
<h2>State Rep. Lee: Consideration of changes to ADPH, State Health Officer won’t come until 2022 session</h2>
</div>
<div class="post-image" style="background-image: url('https://yellowhammernews.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Lee326.jpg');"></div>
<span class="caption">(WDHN/YouTube)</span>
<div class="post-content" data-ids="">
<div class="text-small brief_body test1 test19">
<p>Last month, State Sen. Jim McClendon (R-Springville) introduced <a href="http://alisondb.legislature.state.al.us/ALISON/SearchableInstruments/2021RS/PrintFiles/SB240-int.pdf">legislation</a> that would reconstitute the Alabama Department of Public Health (ADPH) and remake the agency’s leadership. McClendon, the chairman of the State Senate Health Committee, proposed abolishing the State Board of Health and the State Health Officer. Also included in his proposal would be creating a Secretary of the Alabama Department of Public Health, which the Governor would appoint.</p>
<p>McClendon’s counterpart in the House of Representatives, House Health Committee chairman State Rep. Paul Lee (R-Dothan) is also considering options to deal with the agency and the role of the State Health Officer, an office currently occupied by Dr. Scott Harris. However, Lee does not think a fair evaluation of the ADPH can be made under the current circumstances of the COVID-19 pandemic.</p>
<p>Lee explained his preference to wait until the 2022 legislative session to consider changes to the state government executive branch’s role in public health during an appearance on Mobile radio FM Talk 106.5’s “The Jeff Poor Show.”</p>
<!-- <pre> -->
<!-- </pre> -->
<div id="count_words" style="display: none!important;">

                                            322</div>
<div class="button-wrapper">
<a class="view-more1" href="javascript:void(0)">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">322 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
<div class="dv" style="display: none;"></div>
<div class="button-wrapper" style="display: none;">
<a class="view-more" href="https://yellowhammernews.com/state-rep-lee-consideration-of-changes-to-adph-state-health-officer-wont-come-until-2022-session/">
<span><i aria-hidden="true" class="fa fa-angle-down"></i></span>
<span class="keep-reading">Keep reading</span>
<span class="count">322 WORDS</span>
</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="text-large full_body">
<p>
<p><iframe frameborder="0" height="300" scrolling="no" src="https://embeds.audioboom.com/posts/7830455/embed/v4" style="background-color: transparent; display: block; padding: 0; max-width: 700px;" title="Audioboom player" width="100%"></iframe></p>
<p>“I’m actually working with them, presently,” he said. “I think we may have something we can present next year that will address some of the concerns that are out there, and hopefully, we can make it better. It’s worked for 150 years. Do I think we need to scrap it completely? No. But could there be some adjustments? Yes, and I think we’re going to work on that — well, I know we are. I just had some conversations yesterday to see if we can’t bring it back next year because as far as it being in the middle of a pandemic that we’re trying to get ourselves out of — changing courses completely would not be a good idea.”</p>
<p>Lee argued a better assessment could be made with a complete view of information that might not yet be available.</p>
<p>“[I] have concern with someone making the type decisions he is making that answers to someone politically because I’ve seen decisions that were made that I’m not sure I would have agreed with at the time,” Lee added. “But looking back, I’m thinking he made the right decision because he had more information than I had. And you know, I’m hearing from different groups here one way or the other, supportive or non-supportive. You know, I think I have a lot of information, but sometimes I know I don’t have the information as he would have nor the background in medical education that he has. So, you have to have someone there that’s willing to step out and make a decision and have the information to back up that decision.”</p>
<p><strong><em><a href="http://twitter.com/jeff_poor">@Jeff_Poor</a> is a graduate of Auburn University and the University of South Alabama, the editor of <a href="https://www.breitbart.com/clips">Breitbart TV</a>, a columnist for Mobile’s <a href="https://lagniappemobile.com/category/commentary/beltway/">Lagniappe Weekly</a>, and host of Mobile’s “The Jeff Poor Show” from 9 a.m.-12 p.m. <a href="http://www.fmtalk1065.com/">on FM Talk 106.5</a>.</em></strong></p>
</p>
